Of the cauterization of ulcers.
An ulcer is a corruption that walks through the limb, which corrodes it as fire consumes dry wood.
Therefore, if you see the ulcer in a place where it can withstand cautery with fire, then heat up the cautery nails very few and large, according to what is appropriate for that place where it is ulcerated.
Then cauterize all around until you have completely eradicated the entire ulcer and left no trace of it.
Then leave it for three days, and cover the cauterized places with a mixture of olive oil, until all the scabs are removed and all corruption is eliminated.
Then treat it with flesh-generating ointments.
But if after three days you see that healthy flesh is growing in the place where there was no corruption, then it is good; but if not, then repeat the cautery on those places where there is still corruption.
And it is treated sometimes with sharp medicine, because that is used in place of a cautery. But nevertheless, the cautery with fire is a more effective remedy.
And I have already mentioned the treatment for it with sharp medicine in the division, and therefore take that when you will begin with him.
Chapter .53.
On cautery of veins and other similar things.
Many times it is seen that in the parts below the sick foot, which is called a vein, and it is large and deep, which enters the foot; and cautery in these is done in two ways, that is cautery with fire and cautery with hot water.

Then place that red-hot (ignit) on the vein, and then turn your hand with the cautery around the circumference of the vein until the cautery reaches the depth of the vein. Chapter 57.
About the cleansing of infants and the care for those who have undergone circumcision.
Circumcision is not the cure for any other diseases like other afflictions; however, since it depends on our actions and will, and especially because infants are subject to it, it is necessary that we establish the best practice and the easiest way to preserve their health.

Chapter 69
About castration.
Know that castration in our law is forbidden, but I have heard of it for reasons that I remember here in this book; and the remembrance of it is not necessary except in two ways. One way is so that this is in the knowledge of the doctor when he is asked about it, that he knows the cure for those to whom it happens; and the other way is that we have often had need of castration of other animals for our benefit from them, such as mules, and goats, and pigs, and similar animals.
And so I say that castration is done in two ways: either by traction or by incision and amputation.
But in the case done by traction, the procedure is that we castrate the animal in hot water until its testicles are softened and loosened and hang down. Then take those with your hand until they are resolved and do not appear below the touch.
But in castration done by incision and amputation, it is necessary that you hold the animal and press its tail with your left hand.
Then tie off the suspensory ligaments, and make an incision on each testicle with a scissor until two testicles are processed.
Then cut those afterwards that you will have skinned each one. And do not leave on those any scab, except a subtle one which is over the vessels.
And this method of castration is better which is done by traction, because traction leaves little or no cause for the testicles to cause the animal to desire heat [i.e., it reduces the risk of infection and inflammation].
Then heal the wound until it is healed.
**CapÃ­tulo 70** (or Chapter 70)
Of the treatment of hermaphrodites.
Hermaphroditism in men occurs in two ways: one is when a scrotum appears between the testicles, which resembles a woman's vulva and contains pubic hair.
And sometimes, from that area, urine is excreted into the space between the testicles.
In women, however, it takes on another form: the woman's vulva appears as two male testicles, slightly smaller than the average size, with an exterior appearance similar to a man's foreskin and two testicles.
And the treatment is of three kinds: two for men and one for women. And it is necessary that you cut off those attached tissues until the swelling subsides, and then treat them as you would for other diseases.
And in the second type of men, where urine exits into the space between the testicles, there is no cure or operation for him.

Second Chapter: On Fractures That Occur in the Head.
There are many types of fractures, and their forms vary, as do their causes. Some fractures are caused by blunt trauma, which shatters the entire bone and leaves a fragment, just like splitting a stick; this type is called comminuted. Or the blunt object cuts through part of the bone but does not penetrate all the way through it; this type of fracture is called a greenstick fracture.
The wound from these two types of fractures can be either large or small. Fractures caused by crushing or tearing forces are due to blunt trauma or falling onto a rock, and they have similar appearances.
And this type of fracture can be either penetrating, approaching the skin that lies beneath the bone; or it can be on the surface of the bone, and the wound from these two types of fractures can be either large or small.
And there is another type of fracture that occurs within the bone itself, in the subtlety of its fibers; for this reason, this type of fracture is called hairline.
And it is a fracture that is caused either by falling or by the impact of stone or similar objects, which makes some splinter of bone enter into the divided depths, and it is made in the concave place as happens to clay pots when they are hit and their entrance is divided into the divided depths.
And this is most commonly found in the bones of humans, such as children's skulls.
And for all these types of bone fractures, they are painful like scattered stars. And I come to mind about all this in its place.

Chapter IV
On the restoration of the jaw when it has been broken.
When the jaw has been broken and the fracture is not caused by a wound, consider whether the fracture is only on the outside and not split into two parts, curving inward. In this case, its cure is easy.
Therefore, if the fracture is on the right side, you should insert your left index finger into the patient's mouth; similarly, if the fracture is on the left jaw, then insert the index finger of your right hand; and with this, push inward the swelling of the fracture to the outer parts with facility, with your other hand from the outside of the bone; with this, you should decentralize it.
And if the jaw fracture is already separated into two parts, then it is necessary to apply extension to both parts according to what is straight until their union is possible.
And if there is a dislocation of the teeth, then strengthen those which you expect to remain with a thread of gold or silver or linen; and then place on the broken jaw a piece of wax, and then place on it a double cloth, and place on the large cloth a star-shaped bandage well made, or a sole of leather equal in length to the jaw; and then tie it above according to how you are accustomed to the tying of it and as is suitable for the application, so that it is not displaced.
And command the patient to rest and be calm, and provide his food in small portions.
And if you think that the shape has already been altered in some way, then take care of it and remove it on the third day; and then correct what has been altered from him and apply a plaster to him with powder of mills, with egg white, or with cumin flour, after you have removed his bandage, and place wool over the plaster.
And when this plaster is applied and attached to him, and the position of the bone is not altered, leave it there, do not remove it until he is healed, and strengthen the fracture; for many times this fracture is healed in three weeks.
And if another time an abscess appears, then administer the same things that we said many times in his healing until he is healed and the abscess is removed.
And if the fracture is with a wound, then consider whether it is a piece of bone separated or splinters, then be careful to remove those splinters with the same water that you use for removing those from instruments.
"And if the opening of the wound is narrow, then you should widen it with a fleam (surgical instrument) according to your need.
"And when you have removed those splinters and nothing remains, then you should cover the opening of the wound if it is large; and if not, place one of the appropriate plasters over it to encourage healing until it is healed.
"Chapter 5
"On the restoration of the collarbone when it is broken.

Based on the pattern and context from the provided lines, here's a translation of the given sentence:
And do this twice according to what we have agreed upon.
Then press the foot towards the thigh for the third time, and you are at the ankle.
Therefore, if it returns in one time or two according to this manner, and you see the foot swell, that is good; and if not, then upon him iterate the operation, for that returns.
But if to you is forbidden the reduction of him with what we have recommended, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and strongly fasten a heavy weight to the ground, which falls between his thighs, and you have already wrapped a cloth around him so that the patient does not burn.
Then let the servant of him hold his thighs, and then another servant extend the foot with his hands or with a bandage that lies on the neck of the foot; and then let each servant stretch against the extension of their partner, and the weight be extending between the thighs of the patient holding that, so that the body of him is not drawn to the parts below beyond its extension.
Then the physician swells the dislocation with his hands, and another servant holds the healthy thigh below, because the dislocation returns easily.
And so when the dislocation returns and its healing is declared to you, then place a poultice and secure it firmly with strong bandages, and bind the foot to the leg with a bandage.
And you should be careful or protect against the nerves located behind the ankle, so that the bandage over it is not too tight and does not press too hard on them.
And then leave it for two days or three; and if the bandage becomes softened, remove it.
And then unwrap it on the third day or the fourth, and forbid the patient from walking for forty days. But if he is forced to walk before that time, there is no certainty that the dislocation will not be reabsorbed and corrupted, and so it may not receive healing.
And if an abscess happens to him, then you should administer what was previously mentioned in the beginning of this treatise, in another section on treatment and application, until it is removed.
Chapter XXXIV.
On the Treatment of Dislocation of the Toes.
It is advisable that he who is dislocated be anointed with a little oil without difficulty; and this should not be difficult, but rather easy.
"However, if the dislocation is in any of the toes on the bottom of the foot, then it is necessary to make the patient sit with their foot on a level surface on the ground or on a table, and let them remain thus as if they were walking.
"And then you stand on your feet, and place your foot on something soft, like the junctures, and then press down with your foot with all your might until it returns to its original position, and you see that it is level and there is no protrusion.
"And then place under the sole of their foot a board that supports the entire foot, which has two handles, and then secure it with decent and firm bindings for three days; and then remove it and let them rest from walking for many days, until it is healed and the healing is assured.
"Chapter XXXV
"Of the types of dislocation that are made with a blow or with a fracture, or with both together.
"When any of these causes occur and you attempt to treat it and restore the patient, many times death occurs.
"And for this reason, one should not presume to treat it unless he is wise in the art, with long experience, merciful and compassionate, cautious, not rash or presumptuous; and at the beginning use medicines that restrain inflammation only slightly, and leave the patient to divine judgment, except for those whom you hope will be saved from destruction, with relief from illness, and in which you perceive some hope. And then immediately strive to make a reduction from him at the beginning of the cause, before an abscess is formed.
And then if the member returns as we wish, administer a regimen that will prevent an abscess and treat the wound with water from the desiccating ointments.
And if the dislocation is with a fracture and happens in the small bones, then you should pierce their surface, and do what we have said previously in simple illnesses concerning water in those places.
And guard and avoid, according to your ability, those things that lead to fear in the pathways, as I have previously instructed you; for this is better for you and more pleasing to your Creator, and it will bring greater glory and health to your body in your time. Thus ends the words of Al-Bukhari, may God bless him. Amen.
